<p><b>Tropical cyclones</b> are named for historical reasons and so as to avoid confusion when communicating with the public as more than one tropical cyclone can exist at a time. Names are drawn in order from predetermined lists and are usually assigned to tropical cyclones with one-, three- or ten-minute windspeeds of more than 65 km/h (40 mph). However, standards vary from basin to basin with some tropical depressions named in the Western Pacific whilst tropical cyclones have to have gale force winds occurring more than halfway around the center within the Australian and Southern Pacific regions.</p>
<p>The official practice of naming tropical cyclones started in 1945 within the Western Pacific. Naming continued through the next few years before in 1950, names also started to be assigned to tropical storms forming in the North Atlantic ocean. In the Atlantic, names were originally taken from the World War Two version of the Phonetic Alphabet but this was changed in 1953 to use lists of women names which were created yearly. Around this time naming of tropical cyclones also began within the Southern and Central parts of the Pacific. However naming didn't begin in the Eastern Pacific until 1960 with the original naming lists designed to be used year after year in sequence. In 1960, naming also began in the Southwest Indian Ocean and in 1963 the Philippine Meteorological Service started assigning names to tropical cyclones that moved into or formed in their area of responsibility. Later in 1963 warning centers within the Australian region also commenced naming tropical cyclones. In 2011, the Brazilian Navy Hydrographic Center started using naming list to name tropical cyclones over the South Atlantic basin.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Atlantic">North Atlantic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: North Atlantic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>By 1950, tropical cyclones that were judged by the US Weather Bureau to have intensified into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> started to be assigned names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATL_Book_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-ATL_Book-2">[2]</a></sup> Storms were originally named in alphabetical order using the World War Two version of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Army/Navy_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Joint Army/Navy Phonetic Alphabet">Phonetic Alphabet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> By 1952 a new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICAO_spelling_alphabet" title="ICAO spelling alphabet">phonetic alphabet</a> had been developed and this led to confusion as some parties wanted to use the newer phonetic alphabet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> In 1953, to alleviate any confusion, forecasters decided to use a set of 23 feminine names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATL_Book_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-ATL_Book-2">[2]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/1953_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1953 Atlantic hurricane season">1953 Atlantic hurricane season</a>, public reception to the idea seemed favorable, so the same list was adopted for the next year with one change; Gilda for Gail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> However, after storms like Carol and Hazel got a lot of publicity during the 1953 season, forecasters agreed to develop a new set of names for 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> However, before this could happen, a tropical storm was declared significant on January 2, 1955 and was named as Alice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> The new set of names were developed and used in 1955 beginning with Brenda continuing through the alphabet to Zelda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> For each season before 1960, a new set of names were developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_July_07_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-GP_July_07-1">[1]</a></sup> In 1960 forecasters decided to begin rotating names in a regular sequence and thus four alphabetical lists were established to be repeated every four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> The sets followed the example of the western Pacific typhoon naming lists and excluded names beginning with the letters Q, U, X, Y and Z.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> These four lists were used until 1972 when the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA), replaced them with 9 lists designed to be used from 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1977, NOAA made the decision to relinquish control over the name selection by allowing a regional committee of the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> to select the new sets of names which would contain male names and some Spanish and French names in order to reflect all the cultures and languages within the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATL_Book_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-ATL_Book-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> decided that the new lists of hurricane name would start to be used in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATL_Book_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-ATL_Book-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> Since 1979 the same lists have been used, with names of significant tropical cyclones removed from the lists and replaced with new names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATL_Book_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-ATL_Book-2">[2]</a></sup> In 2002 Subtropical Cyclones started to be assigned names from the main list of names set up for that year. In 2005 as all the names preselected for the season were exhausted, the contingency plan of using Greek letters for names had to be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005_AHS_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-2005_AHS-4">[4]</a></sup> Since then there have been a few attempts to get rid of the Greek names, as they are seen to be inconsistent with the standard naming convention used for tropical cyclones and are considered generally unknown and confusing to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-5">[5]</a></sup> However the lists of preselected names for the year, are not expected to be used up frequently enough to warrant any change in the existing naming procedure and thus the Greek Alphabet will be used if the list of pre selected names should ever be used up again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_05_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_05-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_09_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_09-7">[7]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Pacific">Eastern Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Eastern Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Within the Eastern Pacific basin between the western coasts of the Americas and 140°W the naming of tropical cyclones started in 1960, with four lists of female names initially designed to be used consecutively before being repeated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1965 after two lists of names had been used, it was decided to return to the top of the second list and to start recycling the sets of names on an annual basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Nov_07_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Nov_07-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1977, after protests by various women's rights groups, NOAA made the decision to relinquish control over the name selection by allowing a regional committee of the World Meteorological Organization (WMO) to select new sets of names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> The WMO selected six lists of names which contained male names and rotated every six years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_August_07_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-GP_August_07-3">[3]</a></sup> They also decided that the new lists of hurricane name would start to be used in 1978 which was a year earlier than the Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Names1979_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Names1979-35">[35]</a></sup> Since 1978 the same lists of names have been used, with names of significant tropical cyclones removed from the lists and replaced with new names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-33">[33]</a></sup> As in the Atlantic basin should the names preselected for the season be exhausted, the contingency plan of using Greek letters for names would be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett-36">[36]</a></sup> However unlike in the Atlantic basin the contingency plan has never had to be used, although in 1985 to avoid using the contingency plan, the letters X, Y, and Z were added to the lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Padgett_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Padgett-36">[36]</a></sup> Since the contingency plan had to be used in the North Atlantic during 2005 there have been a few attempts to get rid of the Greek names as they are seen to be inconsistent with the standard naming convention used for tropical cyclones and are generally unknown and confusing to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_05_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_05-6">[6]</a></sup> However none of the attempts have succeeded and thus the Greek letters will be used should the lists be used up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_05_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_05-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span id="Central_North_Pacific_(Date_Line_to_140°W)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_North_Pacific_.28Date_Line_to_140.C2.B0W.29">Central North Pacific (Date Line to 140°W)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Central North Pacific (Date Line to 140°W)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1950 a tropical cyclone that affected Hawaii was named Able, after a tropical cyclone had not affected Hawaii for a number of years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C1950_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-C1950-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-40">[40]</a></sup> The system was also named Salome by the Air Weather Service Office in Guam, before it became widely known as Hurricane Hiki, since Hiki is Hawaiian for Able.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C1950_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-C1950-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AWS_1950_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-AWS_1950-41">[41]</a></sup> Typhoons Olive and Della of 1952 and 1957 developed within the Central Pacific, but were not named until they had crossed the International Dateline and moved into the Western Pacific basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C1950_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-C1950-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1957_ATCR_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-1957_ATCR-42">[42]</a></sup> During 1957, two other tropical cyclones developed in the Central Pacific and were named Kanoa and Nina, by the Hawaiian military meteorological offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1957_ATCR_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-1957_ATCR-42">[42]</a></sup> It was subsequently decided that future tropical cyclones, would be named by borrowing names from the Western Pacific naming lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1957_ATCR_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-1957_ATCR-42">[42]</a></sup> Hawaiian names were reinstated for the lists during 1979, with 5 sets of names drafted using only the 12 letters of the Hawaiian alphabet, with the intent being to use the sets of names on an annual rotation basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Nov_07_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Nov_07-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHOP_1980_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHOP_1980-43">[43]</a></sup> However, after no storms had developed in this region between 1979 and 1981, the annual lists were scrapped and replaced with four sets of names and designed to be used consecutively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_Nov_07_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-GP_Nov_07-34">[34]</a></sup> Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007 hurricane season</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a> <small>(CPHC)</small> introduced a revised set of Hawaiian names for the Central Pacific, after they had worked with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hawaii" title="University of Hawaii">University of Hawaii</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Studies" title="Hawaiian Studies">Hawaiian Studies</a> Department to ensure the correct meaning and appropriate historical and cultural use of the names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPHC_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPHC-44">[44]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_North_Pacific">Western North Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Western North Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the Western North Pacific ocean, there are two sets of names generally used. The first are the international names assigned to a tropical cyclone by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) or the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> (JTWC). The second set of names are local names assigned to a tropical cyclone by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a>. This system often ends up with a tropical cyclone being assigned two names, should a tropical storm threaten the Philippines.</p>
<p>On January 1, 2000 the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> as the official Regional Specialized Meteorological Center took over the naming of Tropical storms. The names selected by the World Meteorological Organization's Typhoon Committee were from a pool of names submitted by the various countries that make up the Typhoon Committee.</p>
<h3><span id="Names_used_between_1945 –_1959"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_1945.C2.A0.E2.80.93_1959">Names used between 1945 – 1959</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Names used between 1945 – 1959">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span id="Names_used_between_1975 –_1989"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_1975.C2.A0.E2.80.93_1989">Names used between 1975 – 1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Names used between 1975 – 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td>Kulap</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 1963, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA), have assigned their own names to typhoons that pass through its area of responsibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPJAN09_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-GPJAN09-46">[46]</a></sup> Unlike the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>'s standard of assigning names to tropical cyclones when they reach wind-speeds of 65 km/h, (40 mph), PAGASA assigns a name to a tropical depression when they either form or move into their area of responsibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GPJAN09_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-GPJAN09-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Four sets of tropical cyclone names are rotated annually with typhoon names stricken from the list should they do more than 1 billion Pesos worth of damage to the Philippines and/or cause 300 or more deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001PARList_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001PARList-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Should the list of names for a given year prove insufficient, names are taken from an auxiliary list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001PARList_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-2001PARList-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Names_used_between_1963–1974"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_1963.E2.80.931974">Names used between 1963–1974</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Names used between 1963–1974">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Indian_Ocean">North Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: North Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During its annual session in 2000 the WMO/ESCAP Panel on North Indian tropical cyclones, agreed in principle to start assigning names to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales#North_Indian_Ocean" title="Tropical cyclone scales">Cyclonic Storms</a> that developed within the North Indian Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMD_2009_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMD_2009-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> As a result, the panel requested that each member country submit a list of ten names to a rapporteur by the end of the year 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> At the 2001 session of the Panel, the rapporteur reported that seven of the eight countries had submitted their names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> However, India had refused to submit a list of names, as it had some reservations about assigning names to tropical cyclones, due to the regional, cultural and linguistic diversity of the panel members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> The panel subsequently studied the names and felt that some of the names would not be appealing to the public or the media, and requested that members submit new lists of names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-4"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> At the following years session the rapporteur reported that there had been a poor response by member countries in resubmitting their lists of names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-5"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> In response the panel felt that it was important that the work continued and urged the members to copperate and submit their names to the rapporteur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-6"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> The names were subsequently submitted in time for the 2004 session, however, India had still not submitted their names, despite promising to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-7"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> The rapporteur presented the 4 lists of names that would be used with a gap left for India's names and recommended that the India Meteorological Department's Regional Specialised Meteorological Centre in New Delhi name the systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-8"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> The rapporteur also recommended that the naming lists were used on an experimental basis during the season, starting in May or June 2004 and that the lists should only be used until 2009 when a new list would be drawn up for the following ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31st_64-9"><a href="#cite_note-31st-64">[64]</a></sup> The naming lists were then completed in May 2004, after India submitted their names, however the lists were not used until September 2004 when the first tropical cyclone was named <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Onil" title="Cyclone Onil">Onil</a> by <a href="/wiki/India_Meteorological_Department" title="India Meteorological Department">India Meteorological Department</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMD_2009_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-IMD_2009-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32nd_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-32nd-65">[65]</a></sup></p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South-West_Indian_Ocean">South-West Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: South-West Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In January 1960, a formal naming scheme was introduced for the South-West Indian Ocean between Africa and 80°E, by the Mauritius and Madagascan Weather Services with the first cyclone being named Alix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCWGI_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCWGI-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Over the next few years the names were selected in various ways including by the meteorological services of the region for several years at a time, before it was turned over to the WMO's South West Indian Ocean Tropical Cyclone Committee at the start of the 2000-01 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reunion_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reunion-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Names_used_between_January_1960 –_July_1975"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_January_1960.C2.A0.E2.80.93_July_1975">Names used between January 1960 – July 1975</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Names used between January 1960 – July 1975">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tr>
<th>1959–60</th>
<th>1960–61</th>
<th>1961–62</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_South-West_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season" title="1962–63 South-West Indian Ocean cyclone season">1962–63</a></th>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_Region">Australian Region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Australian Region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tropical cyclones in the Australian region are named by one of five tropical cyclone warning centers that each have the right to name tropical cyclones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_TCOP_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_TCOP-127">[127]</a></sup> The naming of cyclones officially started during the 1963–64 tropical cyclone season, with the first name being assigned on January 6, 1964 to Cyclone Bessie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQ_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AUS_DB_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-AUS_DB-129">[129]</a></sup> Female names were used exclusively until the current convention of alternating male and female names commenced in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQ_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-128">[128]</a></sup> Names that cause significant damage within the Australian region are retired by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Meteorology_(Australia)" title="Bureau of Meteorology (Australia)">Bureau of Meteorology (Australia)</a> with new names selected at the bi-annual meeting of the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>'s RA V Tropical Cyclone Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_TCOP_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-WMO_TCOP-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FAQ_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ-128">[128]</a></sup> In 2008, the lists used by the three TCWC centres were combined to form a single list of names.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Names_used_between_July_1963 –_June_1978"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_July_1963.C2.A0.E2.80.93_June_1978">Names used between July 1963 – June 1978</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Names used between July 1963 – June 1978">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Pacific">South Pacific</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: South Pacific">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tropical Cyclones started to be named within the South Pacific, by the New Caledonia Meteorological Office during the 1958–59 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZ_TC_39-69_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-NZ_TC_39-69-152">[152]</a></sup> The Fiji Office of the New Zealand Meteorological Service subsequently started to also name cyclones during the 1969–70 season with Alice being the first name to be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whats_in_a_name.3F_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-Whats_in_a_name.3F-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p><br/></p>
<h3><span id="Names_used_between_1958 –_1970"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_used_between_1958.C2.A0.E2.80.93_1970">Names used between 1958 – 1970</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Names used between 1958 – 1970">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Atlantic">South Atlantic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: South Atlantic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During March 2004, a rare tropical cyclone developed within the Southern Atlantic, about 1,010 km (630 mi) to the east-southeast of Florianópolis in southern Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_March_2004_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_March_2004-159">[159]</a></sup> As the system was threatening the Brazilian state of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_(state)" title="Santa Catarina (state)">Santa Catarina</a>, a newspaper used the headline "Furacão Catarina," which was presumed to mean "furacão (hurricane) threatening (Santa) Catarina (the state)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_March_2004_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-GP_March_2004-159">[159]</a></sup> However, when the international press started monitoring the system, it was assumed that "Furacão Catarina" meant "Cyclone Catarina" and that it had been formally named in the usual way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_March_2004_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-GP_March_2004-159">[159]</a></sup> During March 12, 2010, public and private weather services in Southern Brazil, decided to name a tropical storm Anita in order to avoid confusion in future references.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GP_March_2010_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-GP_March_2010-160">[160]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming#South_Atlantic" title="Tropical cyclone naming">naming list</a> was subsequently set up by the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">Brazilian Navy Hydrographic Center</a> with the names Arani, Bapo, Cari, Deni, and Eçaí subsequently taken from that list during 2011, 2015 and 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SHEM_Review_2010-11_121-3"><a href="#cite_note-SHEM_Review_2010-11-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SHEM_Review_2014-15_125-3"><a href="#cite_note-SHEM_Review_2014-15-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-names_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-names-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<table align="left" class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Catarina" title="Hurricane Catarina">Catarina (2004)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Tropical_Storm_Anita" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Anita (2010)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Subtropical_Storm_Arani" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Arani (2011)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Subtropical_Storm_Bapo" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Bapo (2015)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Subtropical_Storm_Cari" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Cari (2015)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Subtropical_Storm_Deni" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Deni (2016)</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone#Subtropical_Storm_E.C3.A7a.C3.AD" title="South Atlantic tropical cyclone">Eçaí (2016)</a></td>
